     423             : /*
     424             :  *      pqDropConnection
     425             :  *
     426             :  * Close any physical connection to the server, and reset associated
     427             :  * state inside the connection object.  We don't release state that
     428             :  * would be needed to reconnect, though, nor local state that might still
     429             :  * be useful later.
     430             :  *
     431             :  * We can always flush the output buffer, since there's no longer any hope
     432             :  * of sending that data.  However, unprocessed input data might still be
     433             :  * valuable, so the caller must tell us whether to flush that or not.
     434             :  */

     511             : /*
     512             :  *      pqDropServerData
     513             :  *
     514             :  * Clear all connection state data that was received from (or deduced about)

     572             : 
     573             : /*
     574             :  *      Connecting to a Database
     575             :  *
     576             :  * There are now six different ways a user of this API can connect to the
     577             :  * database.  Two are not recommended for use in new code, because of their
     578             :  * lack of extensibility with respect to the passing of options to the
     579             :  * backend.  These are PQsetdb and PQsetdbLogin (the former now being a macro
     580             :  * to the latter).
     581             :  *
     582             :  * If it is desired to connect in a synchronous (blocking) manner, use the
     583             :  * function PQconnectdb or PQconnectdbParams. The former accepts a string of
     584             :  * option = value pairs (or a URI) which must be parsed; the latter takes two
     585             :  * NULL terminated arrays instead.
     586             :  *
     587             :  * To connect in an asynchronous (non-blocking) manner, use the functions
     588             :  * PQconnectStart or PQconnectStartParams (which differ in the same way as
     589             :  * PQconnectdb and PQconnectdbParams) and PQconnectPoll.
     590             :  *
     591             :  * Internally, the static functions connectDBStart, connectDBComplete
     592             :  * are part of the connection procedure.
     593             :  */
     594             : 
     595             : /*
     596             :  *      PQconnectdbParams
     597             :  *
     598             :  * establishes a connection to a postgres backend through the postmaster
     599             :  * using connection information in two arrays.
     600             :  *
     601             :  * The keywords array is defined as
     602             :  *
     603             :  *     const char *params[] = {"option1", "option2", NULL}
     604             :  *
     605             :  * The values array is defined as
     606             :  *
     607             :  *     const char *values[] = {"value1", "value2", NULL}
     608             :  *
     609             :  * Returns a PGconn* which is needed for all subsequent libpq calls, or NULL
     610             :  * if a memory allocation failed.
     611             :  * If the status field of the connection returned is CONNECTION_BAD,
     612             :  * then some fields may be null'ed out instead of having valid values.
     613             :  *
     614             :  * You should call PQfinish (if conn is not NULL) regardless of whether this
     615             :  * call succeeded.
     616             :  */

    2142             :  * Poll an asynchronous connection.
    2143             :  *
    2144             :  * Returns a PostgresPollingStatusType.
    2145             :  * Before calling this function, use select(2) to determine when data
    2146             :  * has arrived..

    2148             :  * You must call PQfinish whether or not this fails.
    2149             :  *
    2150             :  * This function and PQconnectStart are intended to allow connections to be
    2151             :  * made without blocking the execution of your program on remote I/O. However,
    2152             :  * there are a number of caveats:
    2153             :  *
    2154             :  *   o  If you call PQtrace, ensure that the stream object into which you trace
    2155             :  *      will not block.
    2156             :  *   o  If you do not supply an IP address for the remote host (i.e. you
    2157             :  *      supply a host name instead) then PQconnectStart will block on
    2158             :  *      gethostbyname.  You will be fine if using Unix sockets (i.e. by
    2159             :  *      supplying neither a host name nor a host address).
    2160             :  *   o  If your backend wants to use Kerberos authentication then you must
    2161             :  *      supply both a host name and a host address, otherwise this function

    4255             : /*
    4256             :  * PQcancel and PQrequestCancel: attempt to request cancellation of the
    4257             :  * current operation.
    4258             :  *
    4259             :  * The return value is true if the cancel request was successfully
    4260             :  * dispatched, false if not (in which case an error message is available).
    4261             :  * Note: successful dispatch is no guarantee that there will be any effect at
    4262             :  * the backend.  The application must read the operation result as usual.
    4263             :  *
    4264             :  * CAUTION: we want this routine to be safely callable from a signal handler
    4265             :  * (for example, an application might want to call it in a SIGINT handler).
    4266             :  * This means we cannot use any C library routine that might be non-reentrant.
    4267             :  * malloc/free are often non-reentrant, and anything that might call them is
    4268             :  * just as dangerous.  We avoid sprintf here for that reason.  Building up
    4269             :  * error messages with strcpy/strcat is tedious but should be quite safe.
    4270             :  * We also save/restore errno in case the signal handler support doesn't.
    4271             :  *
    4272             :  * internal_cancel() is an internal helper function to make code-sharing
    4273             :  * between the two versions of the cancel function possible.
    4274             :  */
